  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText14461742986876159167" style="display:none">Ryan Dean West is a fourteen-year-old junior at a boarding school for rich kids in the Pacific Northwest. He’s living in Opportunity Hall, the dorm for troublemakers, and rooming with the biggest bully on the rugby team. And he’s madly in love with his best friend Annie, who thinks of him as a little boy.<br /><br />With the help of his sense of humor, rugby buddies, and his penchant for doodling comics, Ryan Dean manages to survive life’s complications and even find some happiness along the way. But when the unthinkable happens, he has to figure out how to hold on to what’s important, even when it feels like everything has fallen apart.<br /><br />Filled with hand-drawn info-graphics and illustrations and told in a pitch-perfect voice, this realistic depiction of a teen’s experience strikes an exceptional balance of hilarious and heartbreaking.</span>

<div id="review_982156870" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/982156870" />
    <a title="Maxwell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1381728-maxwell"><img alt="Maxwell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539318702p2/1381728.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/982156870?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maxwell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maxwell" href="/user/show/1381728-maxwell">Maxwell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1381728-maxwell?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer982156870" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5136875668826253084"><i>Winger</i> is about a fourteen year old boy named Ryan Dean West who plays rugby at Pine Mountain Academy. He is <i>very</i> "teenage boy" if you know what I mean; hormonal, crude, and thinks he's in love with every girl he sees. He also draws some, and those cartoons are integrated right into the text of the novel.<br/><br/>Why am I giving this book a 1 star rating? <br/><br/>I am fine with saying that I just found myself too old for this book. Some people may argue that you can't be too young or old for books, but in this c</span>
  <span id="freeText5136875668826253084" style="display:none"><i>Winger</i> is about a fourteen year old boy named Ryan Dean West who plays rugby at Pine Mountain Academy. He is <i>very</i> "teenage boy" if you know what I mean; hormonal, crude, and thinks he's in love with every girl he sees. He also draws some, and those cartoons are integrated right into the text of the novel.<br /><br />Why am I giving this book a 1 star rating? <br /><br />I am fine with saying that I just found myself too old for this book. Some people may argue that you can't be too young or old for books, but in this case, having a fourteen year old protagonist dealing with some very mature issues, I could <i>not</i> relate. And subsequently, I felt like the issues were handled very poorly.<br /><br />The book started as a 3-star book for me, but as it went on the rating plummeted to a 2-star for most of the book, and finally by the end I was so bothered that it went to a 1-star rating.<br /><br />If you're afraid of anything possibly spoilery, then don't continue reading (unless A.) you've already read this book or B.) you don't plan on ever reading it:<br /><br />This book deals with LGBTQ topics, which I thought were terribly done. The gay friend character in this book was a great guy, very likeable, and that had me optimistically reading on. But then, without spoiling anything, THE ENDING WAS SO AWFUL. Everything works out great for our narrator, Ryan Dean, but the gay friend (I don't like referring to him as this but I don't want to say the name in case you do end up reading it) is used as a freakin' plot device (not unlike the Manic Pixie Dream Girl that also shows up in this book as Ryan Dean's love interest). Literally, the whole novel is Ryan Dean saying how cool he is with his friend being gay, constantly defending his not-gayness whenever he has a genuine moment with said friend, and then the author exploiting this issue at the end to bring about character development in our narrator.<br /><br />I was honestly appalled.<br /><br />The resolution of this 440 page novel happens in the last 10 pages, so for literally 97% of the novel, Ryan Dean is a one-note, horny, teenage boy, and then MIRACULOUSLY becomes a better person by the end because of this plot point revolving around his gay friend. <br /><br />Besides that, the writing was okay. I'm fine with a little profanity here or there, but this book just had so much in it that was unnecessary and distracting. And on top of that, Ryan Dean says he doesn't cuss in real life, but when he does in the book he reminds you that "it's just what I'm <i>thinking</i>" at the time, but not what he actually said. That got really old, really fast.<br /><br />Was there anything redeeming about this book? Honestly, I'm trying to find something as I type this and the only thing I can think about is that I laughed a couple of times.<br /><br />Sidenote: there is a point in the book where Ryan Dean's mom sends him a box of condoms and a pamphlet about how to have sex for the first time. He is fourteen years old. Now, I don't know about most parents, but I find it <i>highly unlikely</i> that a mother would send her 14 year old son any of those things. Just sayin'.<br /><br />I know a lot of people love this book, but I'm struggling to see why. It's very cliché, and honestly quite offensive at times. I hope that my reasoning justifies this view. Everyone is entitled to their opinion.<br /><br />Peace out.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5136875668826253084" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9886186037304588955">I can't even begin to tell you how good this book was. I wasn't expecting to enjoy it as much as I did. I had issues with the main character, but I like when I have problems with a main character. I enjoy reading about flawed characters. It gets annoying when you read books where the main character is perfect and everybody likes them. The main character in this book goes through a transformation throughout this book and that was really neat to follow. The plot was really interesting and the book</span>
  <span id="freeText9886186037304588955" style="display:none">I can't even begin to tell you how good this book was. I wasn't expecting to enjoy it as much as I did. I had issues with the main character, but I like when I have problems with a main character. I enjoy reading about flawed characters. It gets annoying when you read books where the main character is perfect and everybody likes them. The main character in this book goes through a transformation throughout this book and that was really neat to follow. The plot was really interesting and the book went in a direction that I didn't think it would go. While it's a light hearted and hilarious story, it also has a VERY dark tone towards the end. I would HIGHLY recommend this book, but know that there is crude language and perverse humor. </span>

<div id="review_1433117477" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1433117477" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1433117477?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=masculine-pov">masculine-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=boarding-school">boarding-school</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1433117477" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8523842960265531887"><br/>Ah, Ryan Dean, Ryan Dean, Ryan Dean. He's definitely not your usual contemporary YA hero. Actually, this whole book is a breath of fresh air. Set at a boarding school for both boys and girls, "Winger" illustrates the life of a fourteen-year-old boy in love with his super hot sixteen-year-old best friend, Annie, and his way of coping with being put in the same dorm as someone he's afraid might strangle him in his sleep.<br/><br/>Ryan might come off as an immature, obsessed with the idea of sex and troublem</span>
  <span id="freeText8523842960265531887" style="display:none"><br />Ah, Ryan Dean, Ryan Dean, Ryan Dean. He's definitely not your usual contemporary YA hero. Actually, this whole book is a breath of fresh air. Set at a boarding school for both boys and girls, "Winger" illustrates the life of a fourteen-year-old boy in love with his super hot sixteen-year-old best friend, Annie, and his way of coping with being put in the same dorm as someone he's afraid might strangle him in his sleep.<br /><br />Ryan might come off as an immature, obsessed with the idea of sex and troublemaker kind of guy... and I will admit that a part of him is indeed like that. But in the other part you will find a shy, intelligent and lively boy who has the belief of CARPE DIEM at heart. And did I mention he's an artist? This book is like his journal and sometimes he just likes drawing random (but pretty) images that represent his thoughts or state of mind.<br /><br />I was absolutely engrossed by his adventures and charmed by his feelings toward Annie. I can't say I approve of everything he does or says, because I really don't, but I appreciated his being honest with us and not concealing his opinions. He's a character that will get under your skin, that's for sure. And the best part is that you will like his friends and the other secondary characters as well! Annie slightly gets on your nerve when it comes to her talking about her feelings toward Ryan, and that's why I dropped a star from my rating, but I managed to connect with her.<br /><br />The story is relatively light, even though there are events happening that are not worth laughing over... and especially not the ending... But, overall, you're just going to have so much fun with this book and Ryan. I'm extremely excited to read the sequel because I really don't want to let go of him just yet, especially not after what happened. Hopefully, you'll give this book a chance, too.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8523842960265531887" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer861176345" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12143400940484582789">I’ve got to be brutally honest, I’m not sure why this book has so many glowing reviews and award nominations. Andrew Smith is a good writer, and his truthful, unedited portrayal of teenage boys reminds me of John Green’s <i>Paper Towns</i> (yes, for once, the Green comparisons are actually valid). But <i>Winger</i> is poorly paced and as a feminist and a LGBTQ ally I found Smith’s novel deeply problematic. <br/><br/><i>Winger</i> tells the story of Ryan Dean, a fourteen-year-old junior and rugby player at a boarding school fo</span>
  <span id="freeText12143400940484582789" style="display:none">I’ve got to be brutally honest, I’m not sure why this book has so many glowing reviews and award nominations. Andrew Smith is a good writer, and his truthful, unedited portrayal of teenage boys reminds me of John Green’s <i>Paper Towns</i> (yes, for once, the Green comparisons are actually valid). But <i>Winger</i> is poorly paced and as a feminist and a LGBTQ ally I found Smith’s novel deeply problematic. <br /><br /><i>Winger</i> tells the story of Ryan Dean, a fourteen-year-old junior and rugby player at a boarding school for rich kids. Ryan Dean finds himself dodging teachers and students alike as he attempts to reinvent himself while obsessively pining over his best friend Annie, who only thinks of him as a little boy.<br /><br />Ryan Dean is a fourteen-year-old boy, and there are lots of annoying fourteen-year-old boys in the world. In fact, Smith should be praised for his excellent characterisation, because Ryan Dean is the most frustratingly realistic fourteen-year-old boy I’ve ever read. He’s also grossly misogynistic and ever-so-slightly homophobic and about a thousand times less likeable than I’m sure Smith intended him to be. At no point in the story did I find myself rooting for Ryan Dean, who seems to view his “best guy friend” Joey not as a human being, but as an interesting museum piece titled <i>Gay</i>. It’s apparently impossible for our protagonist to mention Joey without (a) mentioning how gay Joey is and (b) mentioning how absolutely 100% straight he, Ryan Dean, is (just in case the reader hadn’t already caught on from his insistent objectification of every single woman he ever sees). Simply put, Ryan Dean was unpleasant and blissfully unaware of his unpleasantness.<br /><br />I don’t usually have a problem with unlikeable protagonists - in fact, most of my favourite novels have unlikeable or unreliable narrators. <i>Winger</i> had the potential to be brilliant. Ryan Dean was in dire need of a wake up call, and if his character growth had been more satisfactory, I might have understood why everyone else is raving about <i>Winger</i>. But I’m not convinced that Ryan Dean did grow as a person at all. He apologises to the male classmates he wronged, but sees absolutely nothing wrong with continuing to treat the women in his life like prizes to be won. Worse still, Smith lets Ryan Dean get the girl at the end, as a reward for his good behaviour. It’s okay that Ryan Dean has been acting as though he alone is entitled to Annie’s affections, Smith tells his readers, because she was secretly in love with him after all. Rather than write a satisfactory conclusion which shows Ryan Dean’s character growth, Smith takes the story in a completely different direction and ends on a dismissively sensational shocker which eclipses Ryan Dean’s petty concerns and leaves the reader with only ten pages of closure.<br /><br />SPOILERS AHEAD (trigger warning: hate crime, violence)<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Smith’s ending - in which Joey is brutally beaten to death - is emotional manipulation at its worst. Tacked onto the end of a 400+ page coming-of-age story, Joey’s death is reduced to a plot device which the straight protagonist spends only ten pages grieving over - and then just as abruptly healing from. Smith devotes only a few paragraphs to Joey’s murderers and even less words to Joey himself. Instead, the gay best friend character is sacrificed so that Ryan Dean can wallow in self-pity and make Joey’s death all about <i>him</i>. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> It’s sickeningly offensive, and I can’t quite believe that books like <i>Winger</i> are still lauded as “progressive”, while books that actually present nuanced, respectful portrayals of LGBTQ teenagers telling their own stories so often go unheard of.<br /><br /><i>Many thanks to Penguin Books for providing a copy of</i> Winger <i>in exchange for an honest review.</i><br /><br /><b>Publisher:</b> Penguin Books<br /><b>Rating:</b> 1 star | ★✰✰✰✰<br />Review cross-posted to Goodreads</span>
  <a data-text-id="12143400940484582789" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas"><img alt="Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567953607p2/2018505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/642789709?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas">Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Thomas by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/11461398-debbie-narh">Debbie Narh</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer642789709" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15243360488081498904">Unpopular opinion of the day: <i>Winger</i> wasn't that wonderful.<br/><br/>Seeing all the glowing, five-star reviews of this book, I wonder if it's me who went wrong. Andrew Smith did a lot of the little things right in this in <i>Winger</i>. He established a consistent narrative, incorporated rugby and its rules with ease, used a boarding school as the book's setting, and featured a nice friendship between Winger, the main character, and his best friend, Joey.<br/><br/>But I wanted more from this 400+ page book. Several themes</span>
  <span id="freeText15243360488081498904" style="display:none">Unpopular opinion of the day: <i>Winger</i> wasn't that wonderful.<br /><br />Seeing all the glowing, five-star reviews of this book, I wonder if it's me who went wrong. Andrew Smith did a lot of the little things right in this in <i>Winger</i>. He established a consistent narrative, incorporated rugby and its rules with ease, used a boarding school as the book's setting, and featured a nice friendship between Winger, the main character, and his best friend, Joey.<br /><br />But I wanted more from this 400+ page book. Several themes or characters could have been fleshed out with all of that space. Winger and Annie's relationship struck me as false - Winger finds several girls attractive, including Annie, but why do these two like each other besides the fact that they say and act like they do? Winger's personality, while relatable to some, felt stagnant to me, almost as flat as the secondary characters in this novel. It wasn't until the plot twist that took place near page 400 that he showed any real progress beyond just solving a problem or beating someone up. Perhaps if that last event had occurred earlier in the book - it did elevate my rating from two to three stars nonetheless - Winger could have had more psychological development.<br /><br />Overall, <i>Winger</i> was a decent book. I didn't mind reading it, but I didn't particularly look forward to it either. One sweep of the Goodreads page and you can discern I'm in the minority though. If the synopsis interests you, I would recommend reading the first few chapters to see if Winger's voice reels you in. If not, pass.<br /><br />*review cross-posted on my blog, <a href="http://thequietvoice18.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">the quiet voice</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15243360488081498904" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1167235228" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1167235228" />
    <a title="Ɗẳɳ  2.☊" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12058788-2"><img alt="Ɗẳɳ  2.☊" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589380555p2/12058788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1167235228?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ɗẳɳ  2.☊" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ɗẳɳ  2.☊" href="/user/show/12058788-2">Ɗẳɳ  2.☊</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Ɗẳɳ  2.☊ by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn">Edward Lorn</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12058788-2?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12058788-2?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12058788-2?shelf=oh-how-i-loathe-thee">oh-how-i-loathe-thee</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1167235228" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17004090346372671008">Here I am again, the voice of reason, fighting the good fight against a tidal wave of praise and support, in a heroic effort to save you from wasting your precious time and losing your sanity on this dreck. <i>You’re welcome.</i> But I know what you’re thinking, “This is the guy that hates everything, right? How can I possibly trust his opinion?” Well no worries, friendo, because I’m about to break it all down for you. <br/><br/>However, if you’re a teenager or you can relate to or still have the mentality of a </span>
  <span id="freeText17004090346372671008" style="display:none">Here I am again, the voice of reason, fighting the good fight against a tidal wave of praise and support, in a heroic effort to save you from wasting your precious time and losing your sanity on this dreck. <i>You’re welcome.</i> But I know what you’re thinking, “This is the guy that hates everything, right? How can I possibly trust his opinion?” Well no worries, friendo, because I’m about to break it all down for you. <br><br>However, if you’re a teenager or you can relate to or still have the mentality of a sex-crazed, mouthy adolescent, then, by all means, delve in. Feel free to ignore this old man’s rant because I will readily admit that I’m just too old for this shit. I must be a senile old fool . . . cause obvi this book is amazeballs. Winger is like totes adorbs, yo. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1427399925ra/14268564.gif" width="400" height="220" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1388870283ra/7948419.gif" width="400" height="222" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>However, I had a slightly different reaction to the book:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1387902624ra/7695635.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The story follows Ryan Dean West—a teenager struggling through a rough patch in life—while he grumbles about the challenges of life as a pathetic-fourteen-year-old-skinny-ass-fucking-loser-with-no-social-skills. <i>Oh yeah, he likes to hyphenate everything, by the way.</i> <br><br>Now, allow me a moment to lay out a few facts to help put his attitude in perspective. <br><br>Fact #1, he’s enrolled at an uber elite boarding school in the Pacific Northwest where the students are so rich they hop planes to fly home every weekend. Fact #2, Ryan Dean is so smart he’s already skipped a couple of grades. Fact #3, he’s the starting <i>Winger</i> for the varsity rugby squad. Fact #4, he’s so adorable all the girls just want to eat him up. <br><br>Okay, here’s a dilemma, with the proverbial pick of the litter, which girl should he choose? His best friend, Annie, or should try to sweet talk his roommate’s girlfriend instead? Hmm, tough call, Ryan Dean, that’s a real Sophie’s Choice, buddy. <b>#firstworldproblems</b><br><br>God, he’s such a spoiled little brat, even his name annoyed me. In my view, only an irate mother yelling at her kid to clean up their room or take out the trash should ever address a teen by two names. Grow up, Ryan!<br> <br>The story was crafted in a lighthearted, humorous way, but far too often I thought the humor fell flat. Like the scene where Winger was bullied into a late-night, high-stakes poker match. High stakes because they’ll be expelled if they’re caught. <i>Wow, seriously?</i> During the match, he’s pressured into drinking his first beer, so, naturally, he’s drunk from that single beer. <i>Sure, why not.</i> Then, he’s the first one knocked out so now he’ll have to face the consequences. Previous first men out were dared to skinny dip in the lake or run across the football field in nothing but boxer shorts. <i>Ooh, scary.</i> So what audacious challenge do you suppose they’ll put to young Winger . . . ? They dare him to go downstairs to the vacant girls’ dormitory and pee in their bathroom. <i>Wait, what? That’s it?</i><br><br>And therein lies the problem. The story was just so vapid. What’s the point of any of it? *Shakes Magic 8 Ball* “Unclear, ask again later.”<br><br>❅Winger’s roommate’s a bully, or is he?<br>❅You’re so beautiful, Annie. Stop, Ryan Dean, let’s just be friends.<br>❅Insert love triangle.<br>❅Sprinkle in a few amusing pratfalls.<br><br>The rugby matches could have been a nice place to inject some much-needed action and excitement into the story, but no. They were entirely glossed over. All the games were merely preseason scrimmages. The bus rides to the matches were more entertaining than the games themselves. And I still don’t even understand how the game is played.<br><br>Granted, you don’t have to write a mystery, thriller, or some conspiracy theory to keep me engaged in the story. But, for the love of Pete, could you please provide some level of intrigue? <b>Something that I can sink my dentures into.</b> Something other than all this teen angst bullshit! Ugh.<br><br>And stop with the nonsense that I’m too old to enjoy YA because I loved Harry Potter. The sense of wonder was awe-inspiring; the stakes were sky-high. And I thought <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18666047.Half_a_King__Shattered_Sea___1_" title="Half a King (Shattered Sea, #1) by Joe Abercrombie" rel="nofollow noopener">Half a King</a> was a terrific action-adventure, chock-full of clever twists and turns, betrayals and revenge. And the level of gore in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17571466.The_Troop" title="The Troop by Nick Cutter" rel="nofollow noopener">The Troop</a> made my stomach clench, my body shake, my mind scream, “Pass the brain bleach!” For God’s sake Winger, give me something! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427399925i/14268565._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="295" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There was an air of authenticity to the writing at least. That is to say, it appeared to be written by a teenager, at maybe an eighth-grade level, with all of the crude dialog and topics you’d expect. Smith really nailed that voice, but oddly enough, the few adults in the story sounded the exact same.<br><br>Maybe the best way I could describe this book is that it felt like a mashup of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9010.I_Hope_They_Serve_Beer_in_Hell__Tucker_Max___1_" title="I Hope They Serve Beer in Hell (Tucker Max, #1) by Tucker Max" rel="nofollow noopener">I Hope They Serve Beer in Hell</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/99561.Looking_for_Alaska" title="Looking for Alaska by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">Looking for Alaska</a>—two books that I absolutely despised. So, I’m sorry, but this book didn’t work for me on any level.<br><br>And finally, the way in which the author used a gay character arc <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[as a plot device to instill some much-needed growth and maturity in Ryan Dean was deplorable. This all happened in the final few pages of the book. So for 99% of the story, Ryan Dean acts like a complete jackass—incessantly whining about what a pathetic loser he is—then tragedy strikes, and boom - he’s all grown up. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>I think I’ll leave you with a verse from MCA (RIP) that succinctly encapsulated my reading experience:<br><br><i>Pass me the scalpel, I’ll make an incision<br>I’ll cut off the part of your brain that does the bitching<br>Put it in formaldehyde and put it on the shelf<br>And you can show it to your friends and say that’s my old self</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427399925i/14268566.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="17004090346372671008" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/671902579?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tif" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tif" href="/user/show/5524914-tif">Tif</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer671902579" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4698358787954350111">What-if-I-were-to-write-my-entire-review-like-this-in-a-hyphen-abusing-sort-of-way? Would-it-annoy-you-nearly-as-much-as-reading-several-sentences-like-this-on-every-single-page-of-the-book-annoyed-me? Let's-try-it:<br/><br/>Ryan-Dean-is-many-things. Would-it-annoy-you-nearly-as-much-as-reading-several-sentences-like-this-on-every-single-page-of-the-book-annoyed-me? Let's-try-it:<br /><br />Ryan-Dean-is-many-things. He-is-a-stupid-name-and-an-unlikeable-protagonist. He-is-the-author-of-his-own-troubles. He-is-a-loser, he-is-a-skinny-bitch-ass, and-he-is-not-gay. Annoyed-yet?<br /><br />Other things he will repeatedly remind you of:<br /><br />* He is okay with guys who are gay.<br />* All three of the girls in his school are hot.<br />* His one female teacher is hot. As is the one female nurse.<br />* The woman (teacher?) living in his dorm hall is unhot and probably a witch. And unhot.<br />* He is a kid. All of two whopping years younger than the rest of his classmates.<br /><br />Seriously, Ryan Deal will never ever let you forget these facts about himself. On every single page.<br /><br />But as bad as this all may (or may not) sound to you, it was a tolerably light read with the occasional bout of legitimate humor. That is until about the last 20 or so pages at the end of the book. Had I known how it would end I would never have read it in the first place.</span>

<div id="review_467514393" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/467514393" />
    <a title="Shaun Hutchinson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2870295-shaun-hutchinson"><img alt="Shaun Hutchinson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1387295315p2/2870295.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/467514393?book_show_action=true">Dec 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shaun Hutchinson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shaun Hutchinson" href="/user/show/2870295-shaun-hutchinson">Shaun Hutchinson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer467514393" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9108773346701721226">I don't know how to review a book like Winger. I've loved every single one of Andrew Smith's books. Some more that others. But each one has offered up something honest and real and beautiful. Winger is different. <br/><br/>I read in the NYT's review that Winger belongs to a group of books that are all very John Green in nature. And while John Green is certainly a talented writer, I think he writes the kinds of teenagers that adults wish teenagers were. Andrew Smith, on the other hand, writes teenagers as </span>
  <span id="freeText9108773346701721226" style="display:none">I don't know how to review a book like Winger. I've loved every single one of Andrew Smith's books. Some more that others. But each one has offered up something honest and real and beautiful. Winger is different. <br /><br />I read in the NYT's review that Winger belongs to a group of books that are all very John Green in nature. And while John Green is certainly a talented writer, I think he writes the kinds of teenagers that adults wish teenagers were. Andrew Smith, on the other hand, writes teenagers as they actually are. And in that lies his magic.<br /><br />Winger is both perversely hilarious and devastating. I bawled my way through the last twenty pages after laughing my way through the first 410. More than any other book Andrew has written, Winger offers up the harsh truth and beauty of being alive, of being a teenage boy. Of being any kind of teenager. This book has left me feeling really raw. Ryan Dean and Joey and Seanie and even Chas feel like real people. It's strange to think they're not out there somewhere playing poker and giving rides to Screaming Ned.<br /><br />One of the best compliments I ever got as a writer was from a friend who finished one of my books, threw it at me, and told me she hated my guts.<br /><br />Well, I can't throw my book at you, Andrew Smith, but I hate your guts. Thank you for that.<br /><br />Also, if Winger doesn't win the Printz award this year, then I'd seriously question its credibility. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9108773346701721226" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12423312152957980487"><i>“Joey told me nothing ever goes back exactly the way it was, that things expand and contract- like breathing, but you could never fill your lungs up with the same air twice.”</i><br/><br/>The first few pages I wasn't sure I liked it. A hundred pages in I really enjoyed it and about halfway through, I was fed up with the main character: Yeah he's a loser, I get it, I don't need to hear it again. Yeah he's horny, I know, cause apparently everything that walks and isn't male gets his blood pumping. Just tone it </span>
  <span id="freeText12423312152957980487" style="display:none"><i>“Joey told me nothing ever goes back exactly the way it was, that things expand and contract- like breathing, but you could never fill your lungs up with the same air twice.”</i><br /><br />The first few pages I wasn't sure I liked it. A hundred pages in I really enjoyed it and about halfway through, I was fed up with the main character: Yeah he's a loser, I get it, I don't need to hear it again. Yeah he's horny, I know, cause apparently everything that walks and isn't male gets his blood pumping. Just tone it down, thank you very much.<br />Then suddenly, in those last chapters, this hilarious and kind of pointless story got incredibly serious and depressing. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ The death shocked me. And made me mad. I really liked Joey. He was a good kid and he really did not deserve to be killed off like that. Yes, I guess the shocker was intended and was supposed to make the reader think about how this could happen to anybody. Because that's how it goes. Something unexpected and terrible happens and your world comes crashing down. But for me the way this novel ended just did not seem appropriate and it reduced "the gay guy" to a plot point. A dead one, too. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />I have a few issues with this book and I'm not sure it really needs a sequel. I haven't even marked it as to read yet, because I just don't see the point.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer793978137" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16018724530750105173">I don't know if these are spoilers, per se ... emotional spoilers, maybe? Anyway, read at your own risk...<br/>.<br/>.<br/>.<br/>.<br/>.<br/>No. Just...no.<br/><br/>This book didn't earn what it tried to do at the end. And it's so...<i>sensational</i> that it makes me angry, like really and truly MAD, at the author for trying it. <br/><br/>410 pages of dick-and-ball jokes, homo-bashing, and objectifying girls are NOT erasable by a shock ending.<br/><br/>Fuck you, author man. I'm so mad I can't even with this.<br/>*****************<br/>I can see, based on this novel's Pri</span>
  <span id="freeText16018724530750105173" style="display:none">I don't know if these are spoilers, per se ... emotional spoilers, maybe? Anyway, read at your own risk...<br />.<br />.<br />.<br />.<br />.<br />No. Just...no.<br /><br />This book didn't earn what it tried to do at the end. And it's so...<i>sensational</i> that it makes me angry, like really and truly MAD, at the author for trying it. <br /><br />410 pages of dick-and-ball jokes, homo-bashing, and objectifying girls are NOT erasable by a shock ending.<br /><br />Fuck you, author man. I'm so mad I can't even with this.<br />*****************<br />I can see, based on this novel's Printz-nod and unbelievably high average rating here on Goodreads, that I am way, way in the minority on this one. For that reason alone, I solemnly promise that I will gather my thoughts and write a coherent review of this, one that does not involve me sputtering in horror and anger and disbelief. In fact, I disliked this so much that I found myself grinding my teeth in frustration at it all: the characters, the terrible plot, the far-too-frequent mentions of balls, the objectification, and the complete and total lack of the main character having learned a thing. ANYTHING.<br /><br />New goal: work the phrase "Jaw-clenchingly angry" into my review.</span>

<div id="review_721104678" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/721104678" />
    <a title="Ash Wednesday" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10484016-ash-wednesday"><img alt="Ash Wednesday" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379043440p2/10484016.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/721104678?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ash Wednesday" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ash Wednesday" href="/user/show/10484016-ash-wednesday">Ash Wednesday</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781442444942" href="/book/show/13260644-winger">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Readers with an appreciation for comics, Venn Diagrams, bar and line graphs </span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=review">review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=male-pov">male-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=sporty-spice">sporty-spice</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer721104678" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3571929894332183773"><i>
  <b>4 STARS<br/><br/>In this episode of What The F*ck Happened...</b>
</i><br/><br/>Meet Winger.<br/><br/><a href='http://www.flickr.com/photos/99937251@N03/9796172353/' title='image by ashwednesdaylee, on Flickr' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380436846i/883183.jpg' width='420' height='500' alt='image' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Pine Mountain Academy is a school for the rich and the supposedly neglected where Ryan Dean West is a 14-year old junior. The story starts as he begins to serve his sentence (for stealing a teacher's phone) in Opportunity Hall, the school's dorm for the exceptionally delinquent. His day begins by getting dunked in one of the common toilets in O-Hall by two football bullies. Fun times. To make thing more interesting, he is als</span>
  <span id="freeText3571929894332183773" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>4 STARS<br><br>In this episode of What The F*ck Happened...</b>
</i><br><br>Meet Winger.<br><br><a href="http://www.flickr.com/photos/99937251@N03/9796172353/" title="image by ashwednesdaylee, on Flickr" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380436846i/883183.jpg" width="420" height="500" alt="image" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Pine Mountain Academy is a school for the rich and the supposedly neglected where Ryan Dean West is a 14-year old junior. The story starts as he begins to serve his sentence (for stealing a teacher's phone) in Opportunity Hall, the school's dorm for the exceptionally delinquent. His day begins by getting dunked in one of the common toilets in O-Hall by two football bullies. Fun times. To make thing more interesting, he is also bunkmates with Chas Becker (Betch), his rugby teamate who fits the stereotypical dumb jock sketch which also includes <s>wanting to kill him</s> hating him.<br><br>Ryan Dean on the other hand fits the role of the smart, skinny, prepubescent kid who takes a lot of crap for being two years younger than everyone else. But it's the beginning of the school year and Ryan Dean is hell-bent on making some changes and improving his social stock value starting with his best friend Annie who he's been secretly in love with but still sees him as a little boy.<br><br>The story is pretty much several Days in the Life of Winger, where we get to meet his friends, share his thoughts, read about the crazy and embarrassing situations they get themselves into that will probably make Ryan Dean a legend in dinner conversations when he reaches a certain age. But for the here and now, he's 14.<br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>"You look like a gay caveman," JP said.<br>"Well, that wasn't quite the effect I was going for."<br>"Dude. You have Pokemon underwear on."</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br>That wasn't even the funniest bit about the Pokemon briefs.<br><br>Personally, that's like the age I would least like to hear about from the POV of a boy. And <i>Winger</i> pretty much justifies my prejudice. Because Ryan Dean's thoughts were comprised mostly of balls (other people's and his own), sex, pee and rugby. It was all pretty juvenile and awkward at first, then you realize you're witnessing how the primordial male brain works before it evolves irreversibly to this.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380436846i/883184.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Once you manage to keep that in your perspective, it does make Ryan Dean as the narrator easier to take. Because he really is an amusing storyteller who's generous enough to share his thoughts and musings in comic strip form and sketches. He also has this habit of qualifying his emotions and thoughts through bar graphs, line charts, Venn diagrams and scales that I think will satisfy both Barney Stinson and Microsoft Excel fans alike.<br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>Nurse Hickey is a hissing five out of five leaky air conditioning units on the Ryan Dean West Global Hotness Scale.</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br>RD's moments with Annie was very interesting for me because I remember how big a deal a couple of years' age difference is at that point in anyone's life and it isn't something I often read about in YA books from the perspective of the younger, "loser" boy. It was honest and gave me the right kind of warm and fuzzy feels. <br><br>The secondary characters were likable and memorable, their shenanigans absurd (which is my favorite type of shenanigans) and for the first 389-pages you get taken for a Harold and Kumar-type of misadventure (minus the drugs) with a lot of laugh out loud moments that could easily distract the reader from the story it's trying to tell. You KNOW its going somewhere, there's a general subtext of shit waiting to hit the fan, but you don't know where it's coming from. And when you do realize where it's going to come from, you take a step back, look at the bigger picture and not make one sense of it.<br><br>Because when you get to THAT point, that point where Ryan Dean tells you it's just going to be words from then on and no more pictures and graphs, if you haven't been paying attention, you'd really end up pissed off.<br><br>Which pretty much approximated how I felt.<br><br>I was too entertained by Screaming Ned and the TSA kerfuffle that I had to read the final chapters five times and went further back to that fricking Venn Diagram (because seriously, what is UP with the Venn Diagrams YA?! #TFiOS) to make sense of what this book is trying to cut across.<br><br>I'm spoiler tagging my spoilery thoughts mostly because the discovery of what this book was about, I believe is half the fun.<br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Early in the book, Winger shows Annie a Venn Diagram, where the overlap is what makes everyone the same and the small crescent outside the overlap is what makes everyone different. This book tackles that crescent of labels and words and how one overcame his and the other fell victim to his own.<br><i><b><blockquote>And here’s Ryan Dean West. Well, at least, it’s the one tiny part of Ryan Dean West that makes him stand out as being so different, the only thing that everyone notices about him. The number fourteen. And you think that makes me so different, like I’m a little kid. But the thing is, everyone has that little part that’s outside the overlap of everyone else. And a lot of people zero in on that one little thing they can’t get over. Like for Joey, ’cause he’s gay, I guess. Some people are better than others about not getting that outside-the-overlap part so noticed, but not me.</blockquote></b></i><br>It was pretty abstractly presented and nothing gets into sharp focus until the very last few chapters in the end. How Ryan's struggle trying to break out of his label as the "little boy" runs parallel with that of another character until a certain point in the story where they diverge and contrast. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>You know what the other half of the fun is? Coming into this blind. So I'm sorry I wrote this but hey, you've gotten this far in the review so what's another paragraph?<br><br>You could take it for the testosterone humor it so generously gives or the charming love story from the standpoint of the besotted loser but what you can't help doing after finishing this is think. Andrew Smith won't coddle you with a clean, straightforward answer what this is about. He'll take you in a fun, winding seemingly senseless ride, tell jokes, sing a few songs, fall in love... Then throw you into the water without a life vest. You'll wonder what the f*ck happened, you'll feel like you've been stabbed in the back. Then when you've calmed down enough, you will take the pieces that still makes sound logic, fashion it into a makeshift raft to get yourself to a sensible shore.<br><br>If you enjoy that kind of self-abuse, like I obviously do, then come back here once you're done with this and we'll deal with it together.<br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>And then it's always that one word that makes you so different and puts you outside the overlap of everyone else; and that word is so fucking big and loud, it's the only thing anyone ever hears when your name is spoken. <br><br>And whenever that happens to us, all the other words that make us the same disappear in it's shadow.</blockquote>
    <i></i>
  </b>
</i></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="3571929894332183773" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</a><br><br><br>Did I laugh ? Yes.<br>Was there good writing? Yes.<br>Were the drawings pretty ? Yes.<br><br>Those were the only redeemable things about this book.<br>And Joey, the only character I actually liked/cared about.<br><br>Other than that this book was just homophobic and sexist.<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br><br>I didn't care about the cursing nor the constant mention of genitalia or how Ryan Dean was so "perverted". I got that he was a 14 year old boy, I did.<br><br>But where "Winger" went wrong was this:<br><br>1) Ryan Dean was perfectly okay with his friend Joey being gay. He was so okay with it that he had to remind us every time that a) he was not gay, b) Joey was gay, c) He was the only one who was okay with it and d) He did so many "gay" things like hugging his gay friend Joey but he was so not gay!!!! After hearing people praising this book for being a "diverse read" and reading so many scenes like THAT I have to laugh. THAT'S NOT GOOD REPRESENTATION AT ALL. IT'S JUST HOMOPHOBIC SHIT. And then to top all of those homophobic comments, we have the so called ~plot twist~ were Joey dies BEATEN TO DEATH!!! In the last 10 pages or so! And the only "resolution" to this is Ryan Dean talking about how that made HIM feel. Nothing else.<br><br>I do think they were good friends, I LIKED their friendship. Ryan Dean had made some progress with those homophobic comments by the end, but it was SO minor IMO. But there's NO excuse for killing your only gay character to further your MC's man pain, wtf.<br><br>2) All the women in this book existed solely to be classified into "hot" or "ugly" by Ryan Dean. Nothing else happened with them unless they were fussing all over the protagonist. The end. <br><br><s>And there's a sequel coming...</s><br><br>* This book has more than 400 pages, and my first update when I was reading (more than 100 pages in) was this one: <br><br><i>"I want to punch everyone who has recommended this book praising the fact that it has a gay character, because are the others characters even seeing something else past the fact that he's gay ?! (and obvs he's a secondary character) Same with the main love interest, is there more to her that being liked by Ryan ??? I'm hoping this is only because it's the "beginning" of the book. /rant"</i> <br><br>I felt the same way by the end, so there you go.<br><br><br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>This book to me was the embodiment of saying "No Homo" every 5 minutes.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1083095942" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1083095942" />
    <a title="Carole (Carole&#39;s Random Life in Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books"><img alt="Carole (Carole&#39;s Random Life in Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415550632p2/5892196.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1083095942?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carole (Carole&#39;s Random Life in Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carole (Carole&#39;s Random Life in Books)" href="/user/show/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books">Carole (Carole&#39;s Random Life in Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1083095942" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7652617879198487609">This review can also be found at <a href='http://www.carolesrandomlife.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Carole's Random Life</a>.<br/><br/>Why did I wait so long to read this book?!?! I could kick myself for putting this one off for so long. This book has to be one of the best YA novels that I have ever read. It is really that good. I read this book cover to cover in a single day and I can't think of a better way to spend a free day. Of course, I really didn't have much of a choice because once I started reading this story, I simply could not put it down.<br/><br/>Ryan Dean West is in man</span>
  <span id="freeText7652617879198487609" style="display:none">This review can also be found at <a href="http://www.carolesrandomlife.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Carole's Random Life</a>.<br /><br />Why did I wait so long to read this book?!?! I could kick myself for putting this one off for so long. This book has to be one of the best YA novels that I have ever read. It is really that good. I read this book cover to cover in a single day and I can't think of a better way to spend a free day. Of course, I really didn't have much of a choice because once I started reading this story, I simply could not put it down.<br /><br />Ryan Dean West is in many ways an average 14 year old boy. He feels like a loser quite often and he cannot keep his mind off of girls. One thing that sets Ryan Dean apart from the other students at his boarding school is that he is a junior despite the fact that he is only 14. Ryan Dean doesn't let anything stop him. He plays left wing for the school's rugby team, which is where he received the nickname "Winger." <br /><br />Ryan Dean is living in the O-Hall this year because he got into a little bit of trouble the previous year. Opportunity Hall is the residence for trouble makers and Ryan Dean finds himself mixed in with a group of boys who aren't all exactly welcoming. He does make some new friends, finds himself in a few conflicts, and learns to deal with girls during the course of the story. <br /><br />I loved the way this story was told. I absolutely love it when a story can incorporate humor without losing its focus. This book had a thread of humor on nearly every page and none of it felt forced. I never laughed out loud but I was amused for the majority of the story. I really like the fact that the story was not told simply through a narrative. The artwork that was used to help tell the story really worked well and helped bring Ryan Dean to life. I also really liked the way that his thoughts were shown in the story through plays and other creative methods.<br /><br /> This was one of those story that really grew on me. At first, Ryan Dean did seem like an awkward boy who was a little clueless. The more I read the more I grew to like Ryan Dean. He really was a good guy who sometimes lacked direction. I also grew to like his friends. This book really helped me to remember how difficult being a teenager can be. The ending of this book blew me away. I never saw it coming and I am so glad that nobody spoiled it for me. <br /><br />I would highly recommend this book. It was funny and touching in a way that is rarely found in a single story. This is the first book by Andrew Smith that I have read but I am definitely planning to check out his other books soon. <br /><br /><b>Initial Thoughts</b><br />This has to be one of the best YA books that I have ever read. I found it to be both funny and touching. And that ending kind of blew me away. Wow!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7652617879198487609" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_719441474" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/719441474" />
    <a title="Carrie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7190768-carrie"><img alt="Carrie" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/719441474?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carrie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carrie" href="/user/show/7190768-carrie">Carrie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7190768-carrie?shelf=violence">violence</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7190768-carrie?shelf=swearing">swearing</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer719441474&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer719441474" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3677823951474267972"><br/><br/>OK, I never say this, but all I could think as I finished this book was, WTF? Seriously, what just happened?<br/><br/>There are two kinds of terrible books: the kind that you put down after a few pages, because the writing or characters or storyline are awful; and the kind like Winger, that draw you in with decent writing and engaging characters and an award-winning author - and then reward your trust with sloppy plotting and a completely out-of-the-blue ending.<br/><br/>I had a few problems with this book:<br/>1. There</span>
  <span id="freeText3677823951474267972" style="display:none"><br /><br />OK, I never say this, but all I could think as I finished this book was, WTF? Seriously, what just happened?<br /><br />There are two kinds of terrible books: the kind that you put down after a few pages, because the writing or characters or storyline are awful; and the kind like Winger, that draw you in with decent writing and engaging characters and an award-winning author - and then reward your trust with sloppy plotting and a completely out-of-the-blue ending.<br /><br />I had a few problems with this book:<br />1. There isn't a plot so much as a series of episodes strung together - this happened, then something else happened, then something else - there's never really a sense of building to a climax, let alone to what actually happened.<br /><br />2. It's full of comments like this: "...I really liked Joey. But I do mean that in a totally non-gay way." (p.304) What is that? To me it reads as homophobia with a very thin veil of acceptance over top.<br /><br />3. Here's the big one: we have 428 pages of Ryan Dean drinking, fighting, playing rugby, and lusting over everything female, with little to no apparent character growth. There's a bit of tension between Joey and some football players, but nothing that leads you to believe it will cause anything apart from typical bullying behaviour. Then, on page 429, Joey is found beaten to death in the woods. Just like that. That leaves just 10 pages for the aftermath, in which one paragraph - one! - is devoted to the fate of the murderers (they apparently confessed and never came back to school), Ryan Dean cries, people try to comfort him and...that's it. The book is over.<br /><br />It's like the entire book was supposed to be building towards that final confrontation between Joey and the football players - but <br />a) it didn't - I expected them to maybe get in a fight at some point, or for the football players to make some nasty comments, but that's it; <br />b) I wouldn't have even said the aggressors were major characters, and c) we didn't get to see the confrontation/climax. The main character wasn't even involved, apart from getting back to his dorm and thinking something weird was happening!<br /><br />Everything in a story should happen for a reason. To me, Joey's death felt like such a random and unexpected event, and then it seemed like the author barely even touched on the consequences of such a terrible occurrence. <br /><br />This book was very disappointing, and I don't recommend it to anyone.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3677823951474267972" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1052582336" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1052582336" />
    <a title="Edward Lorn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn"><img alt="Edward Lorn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492199506p2/8850418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1052582336?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edward Lorn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edward Lorn" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn">Edward Lorn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1052582336" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1625206961467798532"><a href='http://imgur.com/s3rQGeM' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1410625806i/11133077.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Andrew Smith's Winger flattened me. I was breezing along, laughing and cringing at the shenanigans Ryan Dean West gets into, and then the ending cold cocked me in the feels. Yes, I saw some kind of tragedy on the horizon, but I expected something different than what I received. I was a blubbering mess by the final page. Such a mess that my lovely wife said, "Dude, it's just a book." <br/> <br/>Yet there are some books that rise above simple ink and paper, or collected kilobytes. There are some books t</span>
  <span id="freeText1625206961467798532" style="display:none"><a href="http://imgur.com/s3rQGeM" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1410625806i/11133077.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Andrew Smith's Winger flattened me. I was breezing along, laughing and cringing at the shenanigans Ryan Dean West gets into, and then the ending cold cocked me in the feels. Yes, I saw some kind of tragedy on the horizon, but I expected something different than what I received. I was a blubbering mess by the final page. Such a mess that my lovely wife said, "Dude, it's just a book." <br> <br>Yet there are some books that rise above simple ink and paper, or collected kilobytes. There are some books that breathe. Some novels that are so well written they defy fiction and become real. That's Winger.<br> <br>The cast of characters all have unique personalities, but my standout favorites were Joey, Chas, and Seanie. Ryan Dean was adequate as our narrator, but those three aforementioned teenagers truly stole the show. In my opinion, Chas, as our prerequisite soft-hearted bully, was probably the strongest and deepest character. We hear very little from him other than his constant berating of the rest of the cast, but when things go wrong for Chas it's heartbreaking. I must say, Smith pulled a fast one on me, because I didn't expect to care about Chas. Very nicely done. Joey was my second favorite, and Seanie exists on this list because I've never read about a character like him. Period. He was quirky and hilarious. MySites for EVERYONE!<br> <br>In summation: I'm sorry this review is so short, but I have absolutely nothing bad to say about this book. If you only read one Young Adult novel in your life, make it this one. Funny, endearing, and shockingly tragic, Winger sets the bar for me as far as YA is concerned.<br> <br> <br> </span>
  <a data-text-id="1625206961467798532" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_692744749" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/692744749" />
    <a title="Lauren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4615008-lauren"><img alt="Lauren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579545470p2/4615008.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/692744749?book_show_action=true">Aug 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauren" href="/user/show/4615008-lauren">Lauren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4615008-lauren?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4615008-lauren?shelf=gotten-rid-of">gotten-rid-of</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4615008-lauren?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4615008-lauren?shelf=2016-reads">2016-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer692744749" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer551716498980540044"><a href='http://laurenreadsya.tumblr.com/post/145149590687/review-winger' rel='nofollow noopener'>Check out this review on Lauren Reads YA, with photos of the book!</a><br/><br/>What a piece of crap.<br/><br/>Goodreads is full of 5-star reviews of this book, and I’m honestly not sure if we all read the same book.<br/><br/>The entire book is literally just what I imagine it’s like inside the head of a horny teenage boy. Ryan Dean is fourteen and constantly thinking about ‘hot’ girls, making gross comments at them, sometimes even inappropriately touching them when he gets the chance. Throughout the entire book he objectifies (</span>
  <span id="freeText551716498980540044" style="display:none"><a href="http://laurenreadsya.tumblr.com/post/145149590687/review-winger" rel="nofollow noopener">Check out this review on Lauren Reads YA, with photos of the book!</a><br /><br />What a piece of crap.<br /><br />Goodreads is full of 5-star reviews of this book, and I’m honestly not sure if we all read the same book.<br /><br />The entire book is literally just what I imagine it’s like inside the head of a horny teenage boy. Ryan Dean is fourteen and constantly thinking about ‘hot’ girls, making gross comments at them, sometimes even inappropriately touching them when he gets the chance. Throughout the entire book he objectifies (nearly) every woman he sees. He is called out for this, and he acknowledges it, but no actual character development happens as a result. I’m fine with unlikeable characters as long as they undergo some development, but nothing of the sort happened to Ryan Dean. Still the same objectifying, oversexed, slightly homophobic ass he was before. And most of the ‘humor’ is based on all this problematic behaviour. Like, ha ha, boys will be boys, no homo, I am a pervert, ha ha ha.<br /><br />There is no plot. It’s just Ryan Dean making his female best friend and love interest uncomfortable with his perverted comments, no-homoing his gay friend Joey, complaining about how hard his life is, and picking fights. Nothing happens until the last thirty pages or so, when The Big Thing happens and then it just ends. Probably so that the author could write a shitty, unnecessary sequel.<br /><br />This is on lists as one of the best young adult LGBTQIA books out there, and I don’t see it. There is one openly gay side character, and he seems to be there just to make the main character go through whatever development he needed to go through. It’s exactly the Manic Pixie Dream Girl trope, but even more offensive. The fact that Joey is gay is mentioned <i>constantly</i>, as if that’s the only thing about him worth mentioning.<br /><br />I’m one of the very few people who didn’t like this book, so I wouldn’t recommend it, but I guess it’s a love-it-or-hate-it kind of book, so maybe you’ll love it. I just think the entire thing is wrong, and there are better books about the same issues that wouldn’t be a complete waste of time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="551716498980540044" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
